Talaq — Divorce
beginner
8 min
Permissibility of Divorcing a Pregnant Woman Immediately After Intercourse
Establishes permissibility of divorcing pregnant wife without waiting period

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on divorcing a pregnant woman immediately after intercourse and explain the legal reasoning (dalil) that supports it.

Core Idea
Divorcing a pregnant woman right after intercourse is permissible because her iddah is fixed by delivery and desire remains.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the permissibility of divorcing a pregnant woman immediately after intercourse. The passage clarifies that the usual reason for prohibition—confusion about the iddah—does not apply, and the husband's desire for intimacy is not diminished.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed and the legal classification (hukm). The act is divorcing a pregnant woman immediately after intercourse. The ruling is permissible (mubah).
The core ruling is that no waiting period (fāṣil) is required.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
Find the evidence the author uses. Here it is rational reasoning (qiyās) based on two premises: (a) no confusion about iddah (which ends with delivery), and (b) desire for intercourse does not decrease because it is non-procreative and due to love for the unborn child.
The proof is aqli (rational) rather than naqli (textual).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah (how the proof establishes the ruling)
Explain the logical link. The prohibition of immediate divorce after intercourse for menstruating women is due to potential iddah confusion and decreased desire. Since these causes are absent in the pregnant woman, the prohibition is lifted and the original permissibility remains.
This is an application of the principle that ruling follows cause (al-ḥukm yadūru ma‘a al-‘illah).
4
Note the scope and limits
This ruling is specific to pregnant women. It does not apply to non-pregnant menstruating women, where the prohibition remains. Also, the divorce itself must meet all general conditions of talaq.
The passage emphasizes that the pregnant woman is carrying the husband's child, which increases affection.
5
Evaluate the authority and practical application
The ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah (Hanafi core texts) and is considered mufta bihi (operative for fatwa). No intra-madhhab dispute is mentioned.
Authority weight: zahir_riwayah.

Source Text

حاملہ کی طلاق وطلاق الحـامـل يـجـوز عـقـيـب الجماع لانه لا يودى الى اشتباه وجه العدة و زمان الحبل زمان الرغبة في الوطى لكونه غير معلق اوفيها لمكان ولده منها فلايقل الرغبة بالجماع ترجمہ جماع کے بعد حاملہ (عورت) کو طلاق دینا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ عدت کے طریقہ کے مشتبہ ہونے کا سبب نہیں ہوگا۔ اور حمل کا زمانہ دہلی میں رغبت کا زمانہ ہے اسلئے کہ یہ ولی غیر متعلق ہے۔ یا حاملہ عورت میں (اسلئے رغبت ہے ) کہ اس حاملہ سے اس کا ولد ممکن الوجود ہے۔ پس جماع کی وجہ سے رغبت کم نہیں ہوگی۔ تشریح مسئلہ ... حاملہ عورت کے ساتھ ولی اور طلاق کے درمیان بھی فصل ضروری نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ حاملہ عورت کو جماع کے بعد طلاق دینا جائز ہے۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ حاملہ عورت کے ساتھ وطی کرنے سے عدت مشتبہ نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ کیونکہ حاملہ میں عدت کا طریقہ وضع حمل متعین ہے۔ اور حمل کا زمانہ بھی وہی میں رغبت کا زمانہ ہے دو وجہوں سے ایک تو یہ کہ حاملہ کے ساتھ ولی غیر معلق ہوگی۔ یعنی ایسا نہیں کہ حاملہ کے ساتھ ولی کرنے سے ایک دوسرا بچہ پیدا ہو جائے۔ اور دوسری وطی کرنے سے تیسرا بچہ پیدا ہو جائے ۔ پس جب یہ سمجھے گا کہ حاملہ کے ساتھ ولی برائے تفریح ہے۔ مزید کسی بوجھ کا باعث نہیں۔ تو وطی کی رغبت میں اضافہ ہی ہو گا کمی نہیں۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ حاملہ عورت اس کے بچہ کو اپنے پیٹ میں محفوظ کئے ہوئے ہے اور اپنی اولاد کے ساتھ انسان کو فطری محبت ہوتی ہے۔ لہذا اس بچہ کی وجہ سے حاملہ کے ساتھ محبت میں اضافہ ہوگا۔ اور زیادتی محبت داعی الی الوہی ہوتی ہے نہ کہ مانع عن الوطی۔ پس اس سے بھی ثابت ہوا کہ جماع کی وجہ سے حاملہ کی وطی میں رغبت کم نہیں ہوگی ۔
Divorce of a pregnant woman: And divorce of the pregnant woman is permissible immediately after intercourse, because it does not lead to confusion of the manner of iddah, and the time of pregnancy is a time of desire for intercourse because it is non-procreative, or because in her there is the possibility of his child from her, so desire does not decrease by intercourse. Translation: It is permissible to divorce a pregnant woman after intercourse, because it will not cause confusion in the manner of iddah. And the time of pregnancy is a time of desire for intercourse, because this intercourse is non-procreative. Or in a pregnant woman there is desire because from this pregnant woman his child is possibly existent. So desire will not decrease due to intercourse. Explanation: The issue is that for a pregnant woman, there is no need for separation between intercourse and divorce. Rather, it is permissible to divorce a pregnant woman after intercourse. The reason is that intercourse with a pregnant woman does not make the iddah ambiguous, because for a pregnant woman the manner of iddah is determined by delivery. And the time of pregnancy is also a time of desire for intercourse for two reasons: first, intercourse with a pregnant woman is non-procreative, meaning that it will not result in another child. So when he understands that intercourse with a pregnant woman is for pleasure and does not cause additional burden, then desire for intercourse will increase, not decrease. Second, the pregnant woman is carrying his child in her womb, and a person has natural love for his offspring, so due to the child, love for the pregnant woman increases, and increased love calls for intercourse, not prevents it. So it is also proven that desire for intercourse with a pregnant woman does not decrease due to intercourse.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with its proof: It is permissible to divorce a pregnant woman immediately after intercourse without any waiting period. The proof is that the iddah of a pregnant woman is clearly determined by delivery (until birth), so intercourse does not cause confusion about the iddah. Furthermore, desire for intercourse with a pregnant woman does not decrease but may increase because: (1) such intercourse does not lead to further pregnancy, so it is free from the burden of additional children, and (2) the husband's love for his unborn child increases his affection for the wife, which increases desire. Thus the reason for prohibiting immediate divorce after intercourse for menstruating women (possible pregnancy causing iddah confusion) does not apply here. The ruling is that it is permissible.

Key Terms
حاملہ (hāmila): A pregnant woman.
وضع حمل (waḍʻ ḥaml): Delivery; the end of pregnancy.
غیر معلق (ghayr muʻallaq): Non-procreative; intercourse that does not result in pregnancy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it permissible to divorce a pregnant woman immediately after intercourse without a waiting period?
A) Because pregnancy prevents any harm from divorce
B) Because the iddah is known by delivery, so no confusion, and desire remains
C) Because the husband has absolute right to divorce anytime
D) Because pregnant women are less affected by divorce

Key Takeaway
It is permissible to divorce a pregnant woman immediately after intercourse because her iddah is known by delivery and desire for intercourse does not diminish.

The Sunnah Method of Divorce for a Pregnant Woman: Positions of the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sunna divorce for a pregnant woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the sunna method of divorce for a pregnant woman and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Pregnant woman's sunna divorce: three with month gaps (Shaykhayn) vs. one (Imam Muhammad).

In this lesson, we explore an important intra-Hanafi dispute: when divorcing a pregnant woman in the sunna manner, how many divorces can be given and how should they be spaced? The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) allow three divorces with a month interval between each, while Imam Muhammad (and Zufar) restrict it to a single divorce. This difference arises from how they view the role of months as indicators of need and the nature of the pregnant woman's iddah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
What is being debated? The sunna method of divorce for a pregnant woman: how many divorces can be given and with what spacing?
The issue is not validity of divorce but the recommended sunna method.
2
State the position of Shaykhayn
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: three divorces, one month between each. This is based on the month being a sign of need and desire renewal.
They consider the month analogous to a tuhr for non-menstruating women like ayisa and saghira.
3
State the position of Imam Muhammad
Imam Muhammad (with Zufar): only one divorce, because the month is not an iddah interval for a pregnant woman. She resembles a woman with extended tuhr.
He argues that the original prohibition in divorce requires strict adherence to iddah intervals; months are not valid for pregnancy.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to Shaykhayn, one may give three divorces with month gaps and it counts as sunna; according to Muhammad, only one divorce is sunna, and giving three would be contrary to sunna.
In practice, the mufta bihi is Shaykhayn's view, so three divorces with month intervals are permissible.

مہینہ کا دلیل حاجت ہونا ) اس لئے ہے کہ مہینہ تجد در رغبت کا زمانہ ہے اس بناء پر جس پر طبیعت سلیمہ (واقع ہوئی ) پس مہینہ علامت اور دلیل (حاجت) بننے کی صلاحیت رکھے گا۔ بخلاف اس عورت کے جس کا طہر دراز ہو گیا کیونکہ اس کے حق میں علامت طہر ہے اور وہ ہر زمانہ میں متوقع ہے اور حمل کے ساتھ امید نہیں کی جاسکتی۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر حاملہ کو تین طلاق مسنون طریقہ پر دینے کا ارادہ ہو تو ہر دو طلاقوں کے Sunnah Divorce of Pregnant Woman: And he divorces her for the sunna three times, separating between every two divorces by a month according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: He should not divorce her for the sunna except one, because the original principle in divorce is prohibition, and the Shari'ah has come with separation upon the intervals of iddah, and the month in the case of the pregnant woman is not among its intervals, so she becomes like one whose tuhr (pure period) is extended. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that permissibility is due to the cause of need, and the month is an indicator of need, just as in the case of the ayisa and saghira. And this is because it is a time of renewal of desire, according to sound nature. So it is suitable as a sign and proof, unlike the woman with extended tuhr, because the sign in her case is tuhr, which is expected at any time, and cannot be expected with pregnancy. (Then Urdu explanation) Translation of Urdu: And he gives the pregnant woman three divorces in the sunna manner, separating between every two divorces by a month, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad said: Do not divorce her in the sunna manner except one, because the original in divorce is prohibition, and the Shari'ah has come that divorce should be distributed over the intervals of iddah, and the month is not among the intervals of iddah for the pregnant woman, so she becomes like a woman with extended tuhr. The evidence of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that permissibility is due to the cause of need, and the month is evidence of need, as in the case of ayisa and saghira. And this month being evidence of need is because the month is a time of renewal of desire, according to sound nature. So the month is suitable as a sign and proof, unlike the woman with extended tuhr, because the sign in her case is tuhr, which is expected at any time, and cannot be expected with pregnancy. Explanation: The issue is that if one intends to give three divorces to a pregnant woman in the sunna manner, he should separate between every two divorces by a month, according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Imam Muhammad said: For a pregnant woman, sunna divorce is only one. This is also the saying of Imam Zufar. Imam Muhammad's evidence is that the original rule in divorce is prohibition, and the Shari'ah has come that divorce should be distributed over the intervals of iddah. That is, for menstruating women, three divorces are given over three tuhr periods. And since the Shari'ah has also come that the month stands in place of menstruation for ayisa and saghira, hence divorces are distributed over months, making ayisa and saghira follow menstruating women. But for the pregnant woman, the month is not among the intervals of iddah. So the pregnant woman becomes like a woman with extended tuhr. Meaning, if a woman's tuhr becomes extended, her divorce is not distributed over months, but rather only one divorce can be given in the entire tuhr period in the sunna manner. Similarly, for a pregnant woman...
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage covers an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sunna method of divorce for a pregnant woman. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that three divorces can be given, with a month interval between each, just as for ayisa and saghira. Imam Muhammad (and Zufar) hold that only one divorce is allowed in the sunna manner, because the pregnant woman's iddah is not divided by months (her intervals are not defined by monthly periods), so she resembles a woman with extended tuhr, who can only be given one sunna divorce. The two shaykhs argue that the month serves as a proxy for need and desire renewal, which applies to pregnant women as well, as they too experience renewal of desire. The practical consequence: according to the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), three divorces with month intervals are permissible; according to Muhammad, only one divorce is sunna, and giving three would be against sunna (though the divorce may still take effect?). The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as indicated by the text introducing it as the sunna method.

Key Terms
طلق للسنة (tallaqa lil-sunna): To divorce according to the sunna method, i.e., respecting the recommended intervals.
ممتدة طهرها (mumtaddah ṭuhruhā): A woman whose period of purity (tuhr) is prolonged, e.g., due to illness or age.
فصول العدة (fuṣūl al-ʻidda): The intervals of the waiting period, such as menstruations or months, used to space out divorces.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) One divorce at any time
B) Three divorces with a month between each
C) Three divorces with no gap
D) Two divorces with a tuhr gap

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi position for sunna divorce of a pregnant woman is three divorces with month intervals, based on the month as a sign of need and desire renewal.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate

The Proofs: Analogy and Need in the Sunnah Divorce Dispute
Proof analysis of intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two arguments (dalil) in the dispute and identify the analogy (qiyas) used by each side.

Core Idea
Two analogies compete: pregnant woman as extended tuhr (Muhammad) vs. as ayisa/saghira (Shaykhayn).

In this lesson, we dive into the proof structure behind the intra-Hanafi dispute on sunna divorce for a pregnant woman. Both sides start from the same principles—original prohibition of divorce and the requirement to space divorces over iddah intervals—but they differ on whether the month can serve as a proxy for need and desire renewal, and whether the pregnant woman is analogous to the woman with extended tuhr or to the menopausal woman (ayisa) and minor (saghira). By understanding these analogies, you will see how fiqh reasoning works in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the starting principle
Both sides agree that the original ruling on divorce is prohibition (al-asl al-hazr) and that the Shari'ah has allowed spacing divorces over iddah intervals (fuṣūl al-ʻidda).
This principle is found in the text: 'al-asl fi al-talaq al-hazr wa qad warada al-shar' bi al-tafriq `ala fuṣūl al-ʻidda'.
2
Extract Imam Muhammad's analogy
Imam Muhammad argues that the month is not an iddah interval for a pregnant woman, so she becomes like a woman with extended tuhr (mumtaddah tuhr), who also cannot have intervals based on months. Thus, only one sunna divorce is allowed.
The text says: 'faṣāra ka al-mumtaddah ṭuhruhā'.
3
Extract the Shaykhayn's analogy
The Shaykhayn argue that permissibility is due to need, and the month is a sign of need because desires renew monthly. This is established in the cases of ayisa and saghira, where months serve as intervals. So the pregnant woman is analogous to them.
The text says: 'ka mā fī ḥaqq al-āyisa wa al-ṣaghīra'.
4
Analyze the basis of the Shaykhayn's analogy
They argue that the month is a time of renewal of desire (zaman tajaddud al-raghba) based on sound human nature. Therefore, the month is a valid sign of need and can serve as an interval even for a pregnant woman.
The text mentions: 'wa hādhā li-annahu zamān tajaddud al-raghba `alā mā `alayhi al-jibla al-salīma'.
5
Contrast with the woman with extended tuhr
The Shaykhayn distinguish the pregnant woman from the woman with extended tuhr because in the latter, the sign is tuhr itself, which is expected at any time and not predictable monthly. In pregnancy, monthly desire renewal is expectable, so the month works as a sign.
The text says: 'bi-khilāf al-mumtaddah ṭuhrihā li-anna al-`ilm fī ḥaqqihā innamā huwa al-ṭuhru wa huwa marjūw fīhā fī kulli zamān, wa lā yurjā maʻa al-ḥamal.'

Source Text

الحامل ليس من فصولها فصار كالممتدة طهرها ولهما ان الاباحة لعلة الحاجة والشهرد ليلها كمافي حق الأنسة والصغيرة وهذا لانه زمان تجدد الرغبة على ما عليه الجبلة السليمة فصلح علما ودليلا بخلاف الممتدة طهرها لان العلم في حقها انما هو الطهر وهو مرجو فيها في كل زمان ولا يرجى مع الحبل ترجمہ اور حاملہ کو سنت کے وقت میں تین طلاق دے۔ ہر دو طلاقوں کے درمیان ایک ماہ کا فصل کرے۔ ابوحنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ اس کو طلاق نہ دے سنت کے (طریقہ پر ) مگر ایک۔ اسلئے کہ اصل طلاق میں ممانعت ہے۔ اور شریعت وارد ہوئی ہے ) کہ طلاق کو ) عدت کی فصلوں پر متفرق کرے۔ اور مہینہ حاملہ کے حق میں فصول عدت میں سے نہیں ہے۔ پس ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ وہ عورت جس کا طہر دراز ہو گیا۔ اور یخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اباحت ( طلاق ) علت حاجت کی وجہ سے ہے اور مہینہ دلیل حاجت ہے۔ جیسا کہ آئسہ اور صغیرہ کے حق میں۔ اور یہ مہینہ کا دلیل حاجت ہونا ) اس لئے ہے کہ مہینہ تجد در رغبت کا زمانہ ہے اس بناء پر جس پر طبیعت سلیمہ (واقع ہوئی ) پس مہینہ علامت اور دلیل (حاجت) بننے کی صلاحیت رکھے گا۔ بخلاف اس عورت کے جس کا طہر دراز ہو گیا کیونکہ اس کے حق میں علامت طہر ہے اور وہ ہر زمانہ میں متوقع ہے اور حمل کے ساتھ امید نہیں کی جاسکتی۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر حاملہ کو تین طلاق مسنون طریقہ پر دینے کا ارادہ ہو تو ہر دو طلاقوں کے درمیان ایک ماہ کا فصل کرے شیخین کے نزدیک امام محمد نے فرمایا حاملہ عورت کیلئے طلاق سنت صرف ایک طلاق ہے۔ یہی قول امام زفر کا ہے۔ امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ طلاق میں اصل ممانعت ہے اور شریعت اس پر وارد ہوئی کہ طلاق کو فصول عدت پر متفرق کیا جائے ۔ یعنی ذوات الحیض میں تین طلاق تین طہروں پر متفرق کر کے واقع کی جائیں اور چونکہ شرعیت اس پر بھی وارد ہوئی ہے کہ مہینہ حیض کے قام مقام ہے آنسہ اور صغیرہ کے حق میں۔ لہذا طلاقوں کو مہینوں پر متفرق کرنے میں آئسہ اور صغیرہ کو ذوات احیض کے ساتھ لاحق کر دیا جائے گا۔ اور حاملہ کے حق میں مہینہ فصول عدت میں سے نہیں ہے۔ پس حاملہ عورت ممتدہ طہر کے مانند ہوگئی۔ یعنی اگر کسی عورت کا طہر دراز ہو گیا تو اس کی طلاق کو مہینوں پر متفرق نہیں کیا جائے گا بلکہ پوری مدت طہر میں سنت طریقہ پر ایک ہی طلاق دی جا سکتی ہے۔ اسی طرح حاملہ عورت کو
Sunnah Divorce of Pregnant Woman: And he divorces her for the sunna three times, separating between every two divorces by a month according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: He should not divorce her for the sunna except one, because the original principle in divorce is prohibition, and the Shari'ah has come with separation upon the intervals of iddah, and the month in the case of the pregnant woman is not among its intervals, so she becomes like one whose tuhr (pure period) is extended. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that permissibility is due to the cause of need, and the month is an indicator of need, just as in the case of the ayisa and saghira. And this is because it is a time of renewal of desire, according to sound nature. So it is suitable as a sign and proof, unlike the woman with extended tuhr, because the sign in her case is tuhr, which is expected at any time, and cannot be expected with pregnancy. (Then Urdu explanation) Translation of Urdu: And he gives the pregnant woman three divorces in the sunna manner, separating between every two divorces by a month, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad said: Do not divorce her in the sunna manner except one, because the original in divorce is prohibition, and the Shari'ah has come that divorce should be distributed over the intervals of iddah, and the month is not among the intervals of iddah for the pregnant woman, so she becomes like a woman with extended tuhr. The evidence of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that permissibility is due to the cause of need, and the month is evidence of need, as in the case of ayisa and saghira. And this month being evidence of need is because the month is a time of renewal of desire, according to sound nature. So the month is suitable as a sign and proof, unlike the woman with extended tuhr, because the sign in her case is tuhr, which is expected at any time, and cannot be expected with pregnancy. Explanation: The issue is that if one intends to give three divorces to a pregnant woman in the sunna manner, he should separate between every two divorces by a month, according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Imam Muhammad said: For a pregnant woman, sunna divorce is only one. This is also the saying of Imam Zufar. Imam Muhammad's evidence is that the original rule in divorce is prohibition, and the Shari'ah has come that divorce should be distributed over the intervals of iddah. That is, for menstruating women, three divorces are given over three tuhr periods. And since the Shari'ah has also come that the month stands in place of menstruation for ayisa and saghira, hence divorces are distributed over months, making ayisa and saghira follow menstruating women. But for the pregnant woman, the month is not among the intervals of iddah. So the pregnant woman becomes like a woman with extended tuhr. Meaning, if a woman's tuhr becomes extended, her divorce is not distributed over months, but rather only one divorce can be given in the entire tuhr period in the sunna manner. Similarly, for a pregnant woman...
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage covers an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sunna method of divorce for a pregnant woman. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that three divorces can be given, with a month interval between each, just as for ayisa and saghira. Imam Muhammad (and Zufar) hold that only one divorce is allowed in the sunna manner, because the pregnant woman's iddah is not divided by months (her intervals are not defined by monthly periods), so she resembles a woman with extended tuhr, who can only be given one sunna divorce. The two shaykhs argue that the month serves as a proxy for need and desire renewal, which applies to pregnant women as well, as they too experience renewal of desire. The practical consequence: according to the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), three divorces with month intervals are permissible; according to Muhammad, only one divorce is sunna, and giving three would be against sunna (though the divorce may still take effect?). The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as indicated by the text introducing it as the sunna method.

Key Terms
طلق للسنة (tallaqa lil-sunna): To divorce according to the sunna method, i.e., respecting the recommended intervals.
ممتدة طهرها (mumtaddah ṭuhruhā): A woman whose period of purity (tuhr) is prolonged, e.g., due to illness or age.
فصول العدة (fuṣūl al-ʻidda): The intervals of the waiting period, such as menstruations or months, used to space out divorces.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the effective cause (illa) that Shaykhayn use to justify the month interval for a pregnant woman's divorce?
A) The similarity to a woman with extended tuhr
B) The month as a time of renewal of desire
C) The fact that she is not menstruating
D) The pregnancy itself

Key Takeaway
The Shaykhayn's qiyas relies on the month as a sign of need due to monthly desire renewal, distinguishing the pregnant woman from the extended tuhr woman whose sign is unpredictable tuhr.

Intercourse with a Pregnant Woman During Iddah
Explains permissibility of intercourse with pregnant woman during iddah using rational arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intercourse with a pregnant woman during iddah and explain the two rational bases for this permissibility.

Core Idea
Intercourse with a pregnant woman during iddah is permissible because it causes no iddah confusion and strengthens marital affection.

The iddah period after a revocable divorce generally restricts marital relations, but the Hanafi school makes an exception for a pregnant woman. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its logical justification, showing how the absence of harm and the presence of natural attachment render the act permissible rather than prohibited.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Pinpoint the legal ruling (hukm) stated in the passage: it is permissible (ja'iz) for a husband to have intercourse with his pregnant wife during her iddah.
This is mubah, not wajib or haram.
2
Understand the First Rationale: No Iddah Confusion
Analyze the first argument: a pregnant woman's iddah ends with delivery, so intercourse does not create ambiguity about the waiting period. Unlike a non-pregnant woman whose iddah is measured by menstrual cycles, pregnancy provides a clear endpoint.
Also note that intercourse during pregnancy cannot result in another pregnancy (no 'second child'), so the husband's desire is not diminished by fear of additional children.
3
Understand the Second Rationale: Increased Affection
Examine the second argument: a husband's natural love for his unborn child increases his affection for the pregnant wife, which in turn encourages rather than discourages intercourse. Thus, the act is motivated by positive sentiment, not harm.
This reasoning is based on human nature (fitrah) and is considered a valid rational proof.
4
Recognize the Type of Evidence
Classify the proof: this passage uses rational argument (dalil 'aqli) rather than direct textual evidence (Qur'an or hadith). In Hanafi usul, 'aql (reason) is accepted as a source when no clear text exists, provided it does not contradict established principles.
The absence of a contrary text allows the use of istihsan or maqasid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دینا جائز ہے۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ حاملہ عورت کے ساتھ وطی کرنے سے عدت مشتبہ نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ کیونکہ حاملہ میں عدت کا طریقہ وضع حمل متعین ہے۔ اور حمل کا زمانہ بھی وہی میں رغبت کا زمانہ ہے دو وجہوں سے ایک تو یہ کہ حاملہ کے ساتھ ولی غیر معلق ہوگی۔ یعنی ایسا نہیں کہ حاملہ کے ساتھ ولی کرنے سے ایک دوسرا بچہ پیدا ہو جائے۔ اور دوسری وطی کرنے سے تیسرا بچہ پیدا ہو جائے ۔ پس جب یہ سمجھے گا کہ حاملہ کے ساتھ ولی برائے تفریح ہے۔ مزید کسی بوجھ کا باعث نہیں۔ تو وطی کی رغبت میں اضافہ ہی ہو گا کمی نہیں۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ حاملہ عورت اس کے بچہ کو اپنے پیٹ میں محفوظ کئے ہوئے ہے اور اپنی اولاد کے ساتھ انسان کو فطری محبت ہوتی ہے۔ لہذا اس بچہ کی وجہ سے حاملہ کے ساتھ محبت میں اضافہ ہوگا۔ اور زیادتی محبت داعی الی الوہی ہوتی ہے نہ کہ مانع عن الوطی۔ پس اس سے بھی ثابت ہوا کہ جماع کی وجہ سے حاملہ کی وطی میں رغبت کم نہیں ہوگی ۔
Giving is permissible. The reason is that intercourse with a pregnant woman does not confuse the iddah. Because for a pregnant woman, the method of iddah is determined by delivery. And the time of pregnancy is a time of desire. For two reasons: one is that intercourse with a pregnant woman will be non-consequential. That is, it is not that from intercourse with a pregnant woman a second child will be born, and from another intercourse a third child. So when he understands that intercourse with a pregnant woman is for pleasure, it does not cause any further burden, then the desire for intercourse will only increase, not decrease. The second reason is that a pregnant woman is carrying his child in her womb, and a human has natural love for his offspring. Therefore, because of this child, love for the pregnant woman will increase. And increased love is a motivator for intercourse, not a deterrent. So from this also it is proven that due to intercourse, the desire for intercourse with a pregnant woman will not decrease.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling that a husband may have intercourse with his pregnant wife during the iddah period following a revocable divorce. The author provides two rational arguments to support this permissibility. First, unlike a non-pregnant woman whose iddah is calculated by menstrual cycles, a pregnant woman's iddah ends with delivery regardless of intercourse. Therefore, intercourse does not create uncertainty about the iddah. Moreover, intercourse during pregnancy does not result in a new pregnancy, so the husband's desire is not diminished by fear of additional offspring; rather, it is purely for enjoyment, increasing desire. Second, the husband's natural affection for the unborn child strengthens his attachment to his wife, encouraging rather than discouraging intercourse. Thus, the ruling is based on the absence of harm and the presence of clear benefit. This is a Hanafi position.

Key Terms
حاملہ (hāmilah): A pregnant woman whose iddah ends with delivery.
وطی (waṭʾ): Sexual intercourse.
عدت (ʿiddah): Waiting period after divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because it is necessary for the husband's health.
D) Because the wife must consent.

Key Takeaway
A pregnant woman's unique iddah (ending with delivery) and the natural increase in affection make intercourse permissible during her waiting period.

Sunnah Divorce for a Pregnant Woman: Dispute Between the Two Shaykhs and Imam Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sunnah divorce for pregnant woman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of the two shaykhs and Imam Muhammad on the number of sunnah divorces for a pregnant woman, explain their proofs, and evaluate the qiyas argument from Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
For a pregnant woman, is the sunnah divorce one or three? The answer depends on whether months are considered intervals of need or of iddah.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the proper method of divorcing a pregnant woman. While the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) allow three divorces separated by a month each, Imam Muhammad restricts it to a single divorce. The difference stems from how each views the role of the month as an interval for divorce and the evidence of need (dalīl al-ḥājah). Understanding this dispute sharpens your skills in qiyas and tarjih within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State clearly that the two shaykhs say three divorces with a month gap; Imam Muhammad says only one. Note that Imam Zufar agrees with Muhammad.
2
Trace Imam Muhammad's dalil
He uses the original prohibition in divorce, the requirement to space divorces over iddah intervals, and argues that months are not iddah intervals for a pregnant woman. He draws an analogy (qiyas) to a woman with prolonged tuhr (mumtadatu ṭahrihā) where only one divorce is allowed.
Key argument: the month is not a 'fāṣl' of iddah for the pregnant woman.
3
Analyze the two shaykhs' rebuttal
They argue that permissibility is based on need, and the month is evidence of need (dalīl al-ḥājah), as in the case of a virgin or minor. The ruling revolves around evidence of need, not actual need. They distinguish a pregnant woman from a woman with prolonged tuhr because in the latter, tuhr can be hoped for, while in pregnancy it cannot.
They claim Imam Muhammad's analogy is qiyās maʿa al-fāriq (analogy with a difference).
4
Evaluate the qiyas objection
The two shaykhs respond that the analogy is invalid because the illa (reason) is not the same: in prolonged tuhr, the sign is tuhr (which is hoped for), but in pregnancy, there is no hope of tuhr until delivery. Therefore, the comparison fails.
This demonstrates the Hanafi methodology of rejecting a qiyas when a significant difference exists.
5
Determine the practical difference
If a husband divorces a pregnant woman with three divorces spaced by months, according to the two shaykhs it is valid and counts as three; according to Imam Muhammad, only the first is valid, and the subsequent two are not sunnah and may be considered invalid (bāṭil). The mufta bihi view varies among later authorities.
This thamarah al-khilaf affects post-divorce scenarios like remarriage and iddah.

کا طہر دراز ہو گیا تو اس کی طلاق کو مہینوں پر متفرق نہیں کیا جائے گا بلکہ پوری مدت طہر میں سنت طریقہ پر ایک ہی طلاق دی جا سکتی ہے۔ اسی طرح حاملہ عورت کو اگر طلاق سنت دینا چاہے تو اس کی طلاقوں کو مہینوں پر متفرق نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ بلکہ مسنون طریقہ پر پوری مدت حمل میں صرف ایک طلاق ے سکتا ہے۔ شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اباحت طلاق حاجت کی وجہ سے ہے اور مہینہ دلیل حاجت ہے جیسا کہ آئسہ اور صغیرہ کے حق میں اور حاملہ کے حق میں مہینہ کا دلیل حاجت ہونا اسلئے ہے کہ مہینہ فطرت سلیمہ کے مطابق تجد در غبت کا زمانہ ہے۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ مہینہ حاملہ کے حق میں بھی دلیل حاجت ہے۔ اور پہلے گزر چکا کہ حکم دلیل حاجت پر دائر ہوتا ہے نہ کہ حقیقی حاجت پر اور چونکہ حاملہ عورت کے حق میں دلیل حاجت (مہینہ ) موجود ہے۔ لہذا اسکے حق میں بھی متفرق طور پر تین ماہ میں تین طلاق دینے کا حکم مرتب کر دیا جائے گا۔ بخلاف الممتدة طهرها سے امام محمد کے قیاس کا جواب ہے۔ حاصل جواب یہ ہے کہ حاملہ عورت کو ممتدة الظہر پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں میں فرق ہے۔ فرق یہ ہے کہ ممتدة الطہر کے حق میں دلیل حاجت طہر یعنی تجد دطہر ہے۔ اور اسکے بارے میں ہر زمانہ میں امید رکھی جاسکتی ہے۔ اسلئے کہ ممکن ہے کہ اس کو حیض کا خون آنے لگے پھر اس کے بعد طہر پایا جائے اور حمل کے ساتھ تجدد طہر کی امید نہیں کی جاسکتی۔ کیونکہ حاملہ عورت کو وضع حمل سے پہلے حیض کا خون نہیں آتا ہے۔ پس جب دونوں میں اس قدر فرق ہے تو ایک کو دوسرے پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔
And he divorces her for the sunnah three [divorces], separating between each two divorces by a month according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: He does not divorce her for the sunnah except one, because the original rule in divorce is prohibition, and the Shari'ah has come to separate [divorces] over the intervals of the iddah, and the month in the case of a pregnant woman is not among its intervals, so she becomes like one whose tuhr is prolonged. For them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): Permissibility is due to the cause of need, and the month is evidence of need, as in the case of a virgin and a minor. And this is because it (the month) is a time of renewed desire according to sound nature, so it is suitable as a sign and proof, unlike the one whose tuhr is prolonged, because the sign in her case is the tuhr, and it is hoped for at all times, but cannot be hoped for with pregnancy. Translation: And he divorces a pregnant woman at the time of sunnah with three divorces, separating between each two divorces by a month according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad said: He should not divorce her according to the sunnah except one. Because the original rule in divorce is prohibition, and the Shari'ah has come to separate divorces over the intervals of the iddah. And the month in the case of a pregnant woman is not from the intervals of the iddah. So she becomes like a woman whose tuhr is prolonged... For them (the two shaykhs): The permissibility of divorce is due to the cause of need, and the month is evidence of need, as in the case of a virgin and a minor. And the month being evidence of need is because the month is a time of renewed desire according to sound nature... The detailed explanation: If one intends to give three divorces to a pregnant woman in the sunnah way, he should separate between each two divorces by a month according to the two shaykhs. Imam Muhammad said: For a pregnant woman, the sunnah divorce is only one. This is also the view of Imam Zufar. Imam Muhammad's proof is that the original rule in divorce is prohibition, and the Shari'ah has come that divorces be separated over the intervals of the iddah, i.e., for menstruating women, three divorces are separated over three tuhr periods. And since the Shari'ah also came that the month stands in place of menstruation for the virgin and the minor, therefore in separating divorces over months, the virgin and minor are annexed to menstruating women. But for a pregnant woman, the month is not from the intervals of the iddah. So a pregnant woman becomes like a woman with prolonged tuhr. That is, if a woman's tuhr becomes prolonged, her divorce will not be separated over months; rather, in the entire tuhr period only one divorce can be given in the sunnah way. Similarly, if one wants to give sunnah divorce to a pregnant woman, her divorces will not be separated over months; rather, in the entire pregnancy period only one divorce can be given in the sunnah way. The proof of the two shaykhs is that the permissibility of divorce is due to the cause of need, and the month is evidence of need, as in the case of a virgin and a minor. And the month being evidence of need for a pregnant woman is because the month, according to sound nature, is a time of renewed desire. So it is established that the month is evidence of need also for a pregnant woman. And it has passed before that the ruling revolves around the evidence of need, not the actual need. And since the evidence of need (the month) exists for a pregnant woman, therefore, for her as well, the ruling of giving three divorces separately in three months is established. As for the comparison to the one with prolonged tuhr, this is Imam Muhammad's qiyas, and the answer to it is: The comparison of a pregnant woman to the one with prolonged tuhr is not correct because there is a difference between them. The difference is that for the one with prolonged tuhr, the evidence of need is the tuhr, i.e., the renewal of tuhr, and it can be hoped for at any time, because it is possible that she may start seeing menstrual blood and then have tuhr afterwards. But with pregnancy, the renewal of tuhr cannot be hoped for because a pregnant woman does not see menstrual blood before delivery. So when there is such a difference, comparing one to the other is qiyas ma' al-fariq (analogy with a difference).
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This lesson presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sunnah method of divorcing a pregnant woman. The matn states the positions: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf allow three divorces separated by one month each, while Imam Muhammad limits it to one. The commentator explains each side's reasoning. Imam Muhammad argues that the original rule is prohibition, and the Shari'ah requires divorces to be spaced over the intervals of the iddah period. For a pregnant woman, the iddah intervals are not months but rather delivery; months are not part of the iddah intervals, so she is analogous to a woman whose tuhr has been prolonged, where only one divorce is sunnah. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) argue that permissibility is based on need, and the month serves as an indicator of need, similar to the case of a virgin or minor who do not menstruate. The month is a natural time of renewed desire, so it acts as a sign justifying the spacing of divorces. They further argue that the ruling is based on the evidence of need, not actual need. The commentary then elaborates on the rebuttal: Imam Muhammad's analogy to the woman with prolonged tuhr is invalid (qiyas ma' al-fariq) because in that case, the tuhr can be hoped for at any time, whereas in pregnancy, menstrual blood is absent until delivery. Therefore, the correct position according to the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that of the two shaykhs, though some later Hanafi authorities may prefer Imam Muhammad's view. This passage demonstrates the Hanafi methodology of qiyas and istihsan.

Key Terms
طلاق سنت (talāq al-sunnah): The method of divorce prescribed by the Sunnah, involving spacing divorces over intervals.
فصول عدت (fuṣūl al-ʿiddah): The intervals of the waiting period (tuhr periods for non-pregnant, delivery for pregnant).
ممتدة طهرها (mumtadatu ṭahrihā): A woman whose pure period (tuhr) is prolonged due to absence of menstruation.
دلیل حاجت (dalīl al-ḥājah): An indicator that a need exists, even if the actual need is not present.
قیاس مع الفارق (qiyās maʿa al-fāriq): An analogy that is invalid because of a significant difference between the two cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), how many divorces should be given to a pregnant woman in the sunnah method, and with what separation?
A) One divorce, no separation needed.
B) Three divorces, separated by a month each.
C) Three divorces, separated by one tuhr each.
D) Two divorces, separated by two months.

Key Takeaway
The number of sunnah divorces for a pregnant woman is disputed: the two shaykhs allow three spaced by months; Imam Muhammad allows only one, based on different interpretations of the evidence of need and intervals of iddah.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Divorce During Menstruation: Valid but Sinful, Revocation Obligatory
Ruling on divorce during menstruation: validity, sinfulness, and obligatory revocation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on divorce during menstruation, explain why it is valid despite the prohibition, and identify the basis for the obligation of revocation.

Core Idea
A divorce during menstruation is valid but sinful; revocation is obligatory to minimize the sin.

Islamic law generally discourages and prohibits divorce during a woman's menstrual period. Yet, what if a husband pronounces divorce at such a time? This passage from the Hanafi tradition clarifies that the divorce actually takes effect, even though the act is sinful. The ruling hinges on a key distinction in Hanafi jurisprudential theory: the prohibition is not inherent to the act itself (nahī li-ghayrihī) but due to an external harm, namely the prolongation of the waiting period (iddah). Because the prohibition is external, the divorce remains legally valid. The husband is then obligated to revoke the divorce (murāja'ah) to undo the sin as far as possible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and the Act
Recognize that the passage rules on a specific act: a man divorcing his wife during her menstruation. The act is prohibited (haram) but the divorce itself is valid (sahih). This establishes the foundational legal tension.
Ensure you distinguish between the validity of the divorce (legal effect) and the sinfulness of the action (moral-legal transgression).
2
Understand the Type of Prohibition
The passage explains that the prohibition against divorcing during hayḍ is a 'nahī li-ghayrihī' — a prohibition due to an external factor (prolonging the iddah), not an inherent prohibition (nahī li-dhatihi). In Hanafi usul, an act prohibited li-ghayrihī remains legally effective (mashrūʿ) because the essence of the act is not prohibited.
Contrast with nahī li-dhatihi, which would render the act null (bāṭil), e.g., selling alcohol.
3
Analyze the Proof (Dalīl)
The passage cites the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed Umar to order his son to take back his wife after a menstrual divorce. The imperative 'mur' (command) indicates obligation (wujūb) according to Hanafi principles. This hadith simultaneously confirms that the divorce took effect (otherwise why revoke?) and imposes the duty to revoke.
Note that the proof is a hadith aḥad (single-narrator), which is zannī al-thubūt. Yet the Hanafis treat it as sufficient for establishing wujūb of revocation.
4
Recognize the Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Some early Ḥanafī mashāyikh considered revocation merely recommended (mustaḥabb), but the preferred view (al-aṣaḥḥ) declares it obligatory (wājib). The passage gives the reasoning: to remove the sin as much as possible by eliminating its effect (the extended iddah) and to prevent harm to the wife.
This dispute affects whether a husband who does not revoke has acted neglectfully in a way that requires repentance or makes further rulings more serious.
5
Apply the Ruling to a Real Scenario
Imagine a husband, out of anger, pronounces a single revocable divorce while his wife is menstruating. The divorce is effective — their marriage is severed with the possibility of return during the iddah. He has committed a sin by timing it in this way. He must now perform murāja'ah (say 'I take you back' or resume marital relations) to restore the marriage and remove the sin. If he does not, he remains sinful and the iddah will be unduly prolonged.
The ruling assumes the divorce is revocable (rajʿī) and that the iddah is still ongoing.

Source Text

و اذا طلق الرجل امرأته فى حالة الحيض وقع الطلاق لان النهى عنه لمعنى فى غيره وهو ما ذكرنا فلا ينعدم مشروعيته ويستحب له ان يراجعها لقوله عليه السلام لعمر مرا بنك فليراجعها وقد طلقها في حالة الحيض وهذا يفيد الوقوع والحث على الرجعة ثم الاستحباب قول بعض المشائخ والاصح انه واجب عملا بحقيقة الامر ورفعا للمعصية بالقدر الممكن برفع اثره وهى العدة ودفعا لضرر تطويل العدة ترجمہ اور جب مرد نے اپنی بیوی کو حالتِ حیض میں طلاق دی تو طلاق واقع ہو گئی۔ کیونکہ نہیں (حالت حیض میں ) طلاق سے معنی لغیرہ کی وجہ سے ہے اور وہ معنی وہ ہیں جو ہم نے ذکر کئے ۔ پس اس کی مشروعیت معدوم نہیں ہوگی۔ اور مرد کیلئے مستحب ہے کہ عورت سے مراجعت کر لے۔ ( حضرت ) عمر سے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ اپنے بیٹے کو حکم دو۔ وہ (اپنی بیوی ) سے مراجعت کر لے۔ حال یہ کہ اس نے اس کو حالت حیض میں طلاق دی ہے۔ اور یہ ( قول نبی ) فائدہ دیتا ہے ( حالتِ حیض میں ) وقوع طلاق کا۔ اور رجعت پر آمادہ کرنے کا پھر استحباب بعض مشائخ کا قول ہے۔ اور اصبح یہ ہے کہ واجب ہے حقیقت امر پر عمل کرتے ہوئے اور بقد را مکان معصیت کے اثر کو اٹھاتے ہوئے طلاق کے اثر کو اٹھا کر اور وہ عدت ہے اور تطویل عدت کے ضرر کو دفع کرنے کیلئے۔ تشریح مسئلہ اگر کسی مرد نے حالت حیض میں اپنی منکوحہ کو طلاق دے دی تو طلاق واقع ہوگئی اور بالا جماع طلاق دینے والا گنہگار ہوگا ۔ وقوع طلاق کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حالت حیض میں طلاق سے نہبی معنی لغیرہ کی وجہ سے اور وہ معنی لغیر و تطویل عدت ہے۔ یعنی حالت حیض میں طلاق دینے کی صورت میں عورت کی عدت طویل ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ جس حیض میں طلاق دی گئی وہ عدت میں شمار نہیں ہو گا۔ اور اسی طرح اس کے بعد والا ہر شمار نہیں ہو گا۔ حاصل یہ کہ حالت حیض میں طلاق سے نہی، نہی لغیرہ ہے نہ کہ نہی لذاتہ اور نہی لغیرہ سے مشروع
And when a man divorces his wife during menstruation, the divorce takes effect, because the prohibition against it is due to a meaning external to it (i.e., the act itself is not prohibited inherently), which is what we mentioned, so its legality is not nullified. And it is recommended (mustahabb) for him to revoke it (murāja'ah) because of the Prophet's saying to Umar: 'Command your son to take her back.' This indicates the occurrence (of divorce) and urges revocation. Then the recommendation is the view of some mashāyikh. But the most correct view (al-asahh) is that it is obligatory (wājib) to act according to the reality of the matter and to raise the sin as much as possible by removing its effect, which is the iddah, and to prevent the harm of prolonging the iddah. Translation: And when a man has divorced his wife during menstruation, the divorce takes effect. Because the prohibition of divorce during menstruation is due to an external reason (ma'nā li-ghayrihī), which is what we mentioned (prolonging the iddah). So its legal validity is not nullified. And it is recommended for the man to take his wife back (revoke the divorce) because of the Prophet's command to Umar: 'Command your son to take her back,' even though he had divorced her during menstruation. This indicates the occurrence of the divorce and encourages revocation. Then the recommendation is the view of some mashāyikh, but the most correct is that it is obligatory, acting in accordance with the reality of the matter and to remove the sin as much as possible by removing its effect, which is the iddah, and to avoid the harm of prolonging the iddah. Explanation of the issue: If a man divorces his wife during menstruation, the divorce takes effect, and he is sinful by consensus. The proof of the occurrence of divorce is that the prohibition of divorce during menstruation is a prohibition due to an external reason (nahī li-ghayrihī), and that external reason is the prolongation of the iddah. In other words, when divorce is given during menstruation, the woman's iddah becomes longer because the menstruation in which the divorce was given does not count towards the iddah, and similarly the subsequent one does not count. The conclusion is that the prohibition of divorce during menstruation is a prohibition due to an external reason, not due to the essence, and from a prohibition due to an external reason, the act is not rendered invalid (i.e., the divorce is effective).
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage clarifies a key Hanafi principle: a divorce pronounced during the wife's menstrual period is valid and takes effect (waqū' al-talāq), even though it is sinful (sayyi'a). The reason is that the prohibition against divorcing during hayḍ is not inherent to the act of divorcing itself (lā nahī dhātī) but rather due to an external consideration (nahī li-ghayrihī) – namely, that it unnecessarily prolongs the wife's iddah, causing her hardship. Because the prohibition is not inherent, the divorce remains legally operative. However, the husband is required to revoke the divorce (murāja'ah) to minimize the sin. While some scholars consider this revocation merely recommended (mustahabb), the preferred view (al-asahh) within the Hanafi school holds that it is obligatory (wājib) to revoke, as a means of undoing the transgression as much as possible. The proof comes from the hadith of Umar ibn al-Khattab, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed him to order his son to take back his wife after divorcing her during her menses. This hadith simultaneously confirms that the divorce took effect (otherwise there would be nothing to revoke) and imposes the duty to revert it. The passage also notes that the husband is sinful (āthim) by consensus for divorcing during hayḍ. This is a fundamental ruling in Hanafi fiqh regarding valid but prohibited divorces.

Key Terms
نہی لغیرہ (nahī li-ghayrihī): A prohibition due to an external factor, not inherent to the act itself; the act remains valid (sahīh) but sinful.
مراجعت (murāja'ah): Revocation of a revocable divorce (talāq raj'ī) before the iddah expires.
تطویل عدت (taṭwīl al-ʿiddah): Prolongation of the waiting period, which is the reason for the prohibition of divorce during hayḍ.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the husband's intention overrides the prohibition.

Key Takeaway
A divorce during menstruation is valid because the prohibition is external (nahī li-ghayrihī); the husband is sinful and must revoke the divorce to remove the harm and sin.

Sunnah Divorce for a Pregnant Woman
Intra-Hanafi dispute on number of divorces for pregnant woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on sunnah divorce for a pregnant woman and explain why the Shaykhayn's view is preferred, using the concepts of dafil al-hajah and qiyas ma'a al-fariq.

Core Idea
For a pregnant woman, the month itself is the indicator of need—three divorces in three months are sunnah.

This passage presents an internal Hanafi debate on the sunnah method of divorce for a pregnant woman. Imam Muhammad holds that only one divorce may be given during the entire pregnancy, drawing an analogy to a woman with extended purity (mumtaddat al-tuhr). The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) argue that the month serves as a universal indicator of need (dafil al-hajah), independent of actual purity, thus allowing three divorces spread over three months. Working through this dispute reveals how Hanafi jurists employ indicators and critically evaluate qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Start by clearly stating Imam Muhammad's view (only one divorce throughout pregnancy) and the Shaykhayn's view (three divorces in three months, one each month).
These are internal Hanafi differences; both are based on valid reasoning.
2
Analyze the Shaykhayn's proof
Understand that the permissibility of divorce is based on need (hajah), and the month is an indicator of that need, just as for a menstruating woman. The ruling operates on the indicator, not actual need.
The key principle: 'al-hukm yaduru ma'a al-dafil wujudan wa 'adaman'.
3
Examine Imam Muhammad's qiyas
Imam Muhammad analogizes the pregnant woman to a woman with extended purity (mumtaddat al-tuhr). In that case, divorces cannot be spread because there is no periodic purity to serve as an indicator. Identify the asl, far', and illa in this qiyas.
The illa is the absence of periodic renewal of purity (tuhr).
4
Assess the Hanafi response
The Shaykhayn refute the qiyas by pointing out a critical difference: a woman with extended purity can hope for renewal of menstruation, but a pregnant woman cannot menstruate until delivery. Hence the indicator of purity can renew in the former but not in the latter. The analogy is qiyas ma'a al-fariq (invalid due to a significant difference).
This demonstrates the meticulousness of Hanafi usul in evaluating analogies.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The view of the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school. It is adopted in fatwa and practice.
Imam Muhammad's view is respected but not operative for fatwa.

Source Text

اگر طلاق سنت دینا چاہے تو اس کی طلاقوں کو مہینوں پر متفرق نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ بلکہ مسنون طریقہ پر پوری مدت حمل میں صرف ایک طلاق دے سکتا ہے۔
شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اباحت طلاق حاجت کی وجہ سے ہے اور مہینہ دلیل حاجت ہے جیسا کہ آئسہ اور صغیرہ کے حق میں اور حاملہ کے حق میں مہینہ کا دلیل حاجت ہونا اسلئے ہے کہ مہینہ فطرت سلیمہ کے مطابق تجد در غبت کا زمانہ ہے۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ مہینہ حاملہ کے حق میں بھی دلیل حاجت ہے۔ اور پہلے گزر چکا کہ حکم دلیل حاجت پر دائر ہوتا ہے نہ کہ حقیقی حاجت پر اور چونکہ حاملہ عورت کے حق میں دلیل حاجت (مہینہ ) موجود ہے۔ لہذا اسکے حق میں بھی متفرق طور پر تین ماہ میں تین طلاق دینے کا حکم مرتب کر دیا جائے گا۔ بخلاف الممتدة طهرها سے امام محمد کے قیاس کا جواب ہے۔ حاصل جواب یہ ہے کہ حاملہ عورت کو ممتدة الظہر پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں میں فرق ہے۔ فرق یہ ہے کہ ممتدة الطہر کے حق میں دلیل حاجت طہر یعنی تجد دطہر ہے۔ اور اسکے بارے میں ہر زمانہ میں امید رکھی جاسکتی ہے۔ اسلئے کہ ممکن ہے کہ اس کو حیض کا خون آنے لگے پھر اس کے بعد طہر پایا جائے اور حمل کے ساتھ تجدد طہر کی امید نہیں کی جاسکتی۔ کیونکہ حاملہ عورت کو وضع حمل سے پہلے حیض کا خون نہیں آتا ہے۔ پس جب دونوں میں اس قدر فرق ہے تو ایک کو دوسرے پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔
If he wants to give sunnah divorce, his divorces will not be spread over months. Rather, according to the sunnah method, he can give only one divorce throughout the entire period of pregnancy. The proof of the two shaykhs is that the permissibility of divorce is due to need, and the month is an indicator of need, as in the case of a menstruating woman and a minor girl, and for a pregnant woman the month is an indicator of need because the month is a time for renewal of desire according to sound nature. Thus it is established that the month is also an indicator of need for a pregnant woman. And it has passed earlier that the ruling is based on the indicator of need, not on actual need. And since the indicator of need (the month) exists for a pregnant woman, therefore the ruling of giving three divorces in three months in a spread-out manner will be applied to her as well. As opposed to the qiyas of Imam Muhammad based on the woman with extended purity. The summary of the response is that it is not correct to analogize a pregnant woman to a woman with extended purity because there is a difference between them. The difference is that for a woman with extended purity, the indicator of need is purity, i.e., renewed purity, and hope can be held for it at any time because it is possible that menstrual blood may start flowing for her, then after that purity occurs. But with pregnancy, hope for renewed purity cannot be held because a pregnant woman does not experience menstrual blood before delivery. So when there is such a difference between the two, analogizing one to the other is qiyas ma'a al-fariq (analogy with a difference).
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sunnah method of giving divorce to a pregnant woman. The initial statement (likely Imam Muhammad's view) holds that only one divorce should be given throughout the entire pregnancy, not spread over months. The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) argue that the month itself is an indicator of need, just as for a menstruating woman, and therefore three divorces can be given in three months even to a pregnant woman. They emphasize that the ruling is based on the indicator (dafil al-hajah), not actual need. The passage then responds to Imam Muhammad's qiyas, which analogizes a pregnant woman to a woman with extended purity (mumtaddat al-tuhr). The response refutes this by showing a critical difference: in the latter, renewed purity is possible, but in pregnancy, no menstruation occurs until delivery, so hope for renewed purity does not exist. Therefore the analogy is invalid (qiyas ma'a al-fariq). The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is the view of the Shaykhayn, allowing three divorces over three months for a pregnant woman.

Key Terms
دلیل حاجت (dafil al-hajah): An indicator (such as the month) that signals the presence of need, upon which rulings are based rather than actual need.
ممتدة الطهر (mumtaddat al-tuhr): A woman whose interval between menstruations is so long that she does not have a regular monthly purity.
قیاس مع الفارق (qiyas ma'a al-fariq): An invalid analogy where the two cases differ in a significant aspect that affects the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), how many divorces can be given to a pregnant woman in the sunnah method?
A) Only one divorce throughout pregnancy
B) Three divorces in three months, one each month
C) Two divorces in two months
D) Any number, there is no specific method

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows three divorces over three months for a pregnant woman because the month itself is the indicator of need.

Divorce During Menstruation: Occurrence and Nahy li Ghayrihi
Ruling that divorce during hayd occurs, with proof from hadith and principle of nahy li ghayrihi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a divorce given during menstruation is valid (waqi') in the Hanafi school, using the concept of nahy li ghayrihi.

Core Idea
A prohibition due to an extrinsic factor does not nullify the act's legitimacy.

This lesson clarifies a common confusion: though divorce during menstruation is prohibited, it still takes effect. The key is the Hanafi distinction between prohibitions that target the act itself (nahy li dhatihi) and those that target an external harm (nahy li ghayrihi). Understanding this principle is essential for correctly applying many fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the prohibition
State the ruling: the divorce occurs (waqi') despite being prohibited. Note that the prohibition is not because divorce is evil in itself, but due to an extrinsic reason.
2
Analyze the dalil: the hadith of Ibn 'Umar
Examine the Prophet's command to 'Umar to tell his son to take his wife back. This shows the divorce occurred because raj'ah is only possible after a valid divorce.
3
Apply the principle of nahy li ghayrihi
Explain that the prohibition is for a reason outside the act (prolonging 'iddah), so the act's mashru'iyyah remains intact.
4
Distinguish from nahy li dhatihi
Contrast with acts prohibited inherently (e.g., zina) which are invalid. This classification determines validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و اذا طلق الرجل امرأته فى حالة الحيض وقع الطلاق لان النهى عنه لمعنى فى غيره وهو ما ذكرنا فلا ينعدم مشروعيته ويستحب له ان يراجعها لقوله عليه السلام لعمر مرا بنك فليراجعها وقد طلقها في حالة الحيض وهذا يفيد الوقوع والحث على الرجعة ثم الاستحباب قول بعض المشائخ والاصح انه واجب عملا بحقيقة الامر ورفعا للمعصية بالقدر الممكن برفع اثره وهى العدة ودفعا لضرر تطويل العدة
ترجمہ اور جب مرد نے اپنی بیوی کو حالتِ حیض میں طلاق دی تو طلاق واقع ہو گئی۔ کیونکہ نہیں (حالت حیض میں ) طلاق سے معنی لغیرہ کی وجہ سے ہے اور وہ معنی وہ ہیں جو ہم نے ذکر کئے ۔ پس اس کی مشروعیت معدوم نہیں ہوگی۔ اور مرد کیلئے مستحب ہے کہ عورت سے مراجعت کر لے۔ ( حضرت ) عمر سے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ اپنے بیٹے کو حکم دو۔ وہ (اپنی بیوی ) سے مراجعت کر لے۔ حال یہ کہ اس نے اس کو حالت حیض میں طلاق دی ہے۔ اور یہ ( قول نبی ) فائدہ دیتا ہے ( حالتِ حیض میں ) وقوع طلاق کا۔ اور رجعت پر آمادہ کرنے کا پھر استحباب بعض مشائخ کا قول ہے۔ اور اصبح یہ ہے کہ واجب ہے حقیقت امر پر عمل کرتے ہوئے اور بقد را مکان معصیت کے اثر کو اٹھاتے ہوئے طلاق کے اثر کو اٹھا کر اور وہ عدت ہے اور تطویل عدت کے ضرر کو دفع کرنے کیلئے۔
تشریح مسئلہ اگر کسی مرد نے حالت حیض میں اپنی منکوحہ کو طلاق دے دی تو طلاق واقع ہوگئی اور بالا جماع طلاق دینے والا گنہگار ہوگا ۔ وقوع طلاق کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حالت حیض میں طلاق سے نہبی معنی لغیرہ کی وجہ سے اور وہ معنی لغیر و تطویل عدت ہے۔ یعنی حالت حیض میں طلاق دینے کی صورت میں عورت کی عدت طویل ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ جس حیض میں طلاق دی گئی وہ عدت میں شمار نہیں ہو گا۔ اور اسی طرح اس کے بعد والا ہر شمار نہیں ہو گا۔ حاصل یہ کہ حالت حیض میں طلاق سے نہی، نہی لغیرہ ہے نہ کہ نہی لذاتہ اور نہی لغیرہ سے مشروع لذاتہ باقی رہتا ہے۔ اس وجہ سے ہم نے کہا کہ حالت حیض میں طلاق کی نفس مشروعیت معدوم نہیں ہوئی۔ صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ اس مرد کیلئے اپنی اس بیوی سے مراجعت کرنا مستحب ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب عبد اللہ ابن عمر نے حالت حیض میں طلاق دے دی تو حضرت عمر نے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے اس کے بارے میں دریافت فرمایا تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا کہ اپنے بیٹے عبداللہ کو کم کرو کہ وہ اس سے رجعت کرے۔ اس حدیث سے دو باتیں مستفاد ہوئیں ۔ ایک تو یہ کہ حالت حیض میں طلاق دینے سے طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ اگر حالت حیض میں طالق واقع نہ ہوتی تو ابن عمر گور جعت کا حکم دینے کے کیا معنی ہیں ۔ دوسری بات یہ کہ اس حدیث میں مراجعت پر آمادہ کیا گیا ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ رجعت کے استحباب کے قائل بعض مشائخ ہیں اور صحیح قول یہ ہے کہ رجعت واجب ہے۔ دلیل استحباب یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں فلیر اجحها صیغہ امر ہے۔ اور امر کا ادنیٰ مرتبہ استباب ہے۔ اور یہاں استحباب پر قرینہ بھی موجود ہے۔ قرینہ یہ ہے کہ رجعت خالص شوہر کا حق ہے اور انسان پر اپنے حق میں کوئی وجوب نہیں ہوتا۔ وجوب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مطلق امر وجوب کیلئے ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا حدیث میں بھی صیغہ امر وجوب کیلئے ہوگا۔ پس وجوب مراد لینے کی صورت میں حقیقت امر پر عمل ہو گیا اور جعت اسلئے بھی واجب ہے کہ حالت حیض میں طلاق دینا معصیت ہے۔ اور معصیت کا اٹھانا واجب ہے۔ تفصیل یہ ہے کہ حالت حیض میں طلاق واقع کرنا : معصیت ہے۔ پس مناسب تو یہ تھا کہ نفس طلاق اور مین طلاق کو اٹھا لیا جاتا۔ لیکن چونکہ نفس طلاں کو اٹھا ناممکن نہیں اس لئے ہم کہتے ہیں کہ کم از کم اسکے اثر ہی کو اٹھا لیا جائے ۔ اور طلاق کا اثر عدت ہے پس حاصل یہ کہ رجعت کر کے عدت کو مرتفع کر دیا جائے تا کہ بقدر امکان معصیت کا رفع ہو سکے۔ اور رجعت اسلئے بھی واجب ہے کہ رجعت کی وجہ سے عورت سے تطویل عدت کا نسر ختم ہو جاتا ہے۔
And when a man divorces his wife during menstruation, the divorce occurs because the prohibition is for a reason extrinsic to it (ma'na fi ghayrihi), which we have mentioned, so its legitimacy is not nullified. And it is recommended for him to take her back (yuraji'uha) due to his saying (peace be upon him) to 'Umar: 'Command your son to take her back' while he had divorced her during menstruation. This indicates occurrence (wuqu') and encouragement of reconciliation (raj'ah). Then recommendation (istihbab) is the saying of some mashayikh, and the correct view is that it is obligatory (wajib) in accordance with the reality of the matter, and to remove sin to the extent possible by removing its effect, which is the 'iddah, and to ward off the harm of prolonging the 'iddah. Translation: And when a man divorces his wife during menstruation, the divorce occurs... (Urdu translation follows). Explanation of the issue: If a man divorces his wife during menstruation, the divorce occurs and the divorcer is sinful by consensus. ...
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning divorce during menstruation. It establishes that such a divorce is effective (waqi') despite being prohibited. The reason is that the prohibition is due to an extrinsic factor (ma'na fi ghayrihi) — namely, prolonging the 'iddah — not because the act itself is inherently evil. Therefore the legitimacy (mashru'iyyah) of the divorce remains. The husband is then encouraged to take his wife back (raj'ah). The text presents a debate among Hanafi scholars: Some mashayikh hold that raj'ah is only recommended (mustahabb), while the correct view (asahh) is that it is obligatory (wajib). The evidence for istihbab is that the command in the hadith (فلي راجعها) is in the imperative form, which at minimum indicates recommendation, and there is a qarinah (contextual factor) that raj'ah is the husband's right, and no one is obliged to exercise his own right. The argument for wujub is that a plain imperative indicates obligation, and moreover, giving divorce during hayd is a sin; removing sin is obligatory, and since the divorce itself cannot be undone, its effect (the 'iddah) must be removed through raj'ah. The passage also cites the famous incident of 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar, which proves both the occurrence of divorce and the command for raj'ah.

Key Terms
نہی لغیرہ (nahy li ghayrihi): A prohibition due to an extrinsic factor, not because the act is inherently evil. The act's legitimacy remains.
رجعت (raj'ah): The husband taking back his wife during the 'iddah period after a revocable divorce.
معصیت (ma'siyah): Sin. The act of divorcing during menstruation is sinful but the divorce itself is valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why does a divorce during menstruation occur despite being prohibited?
A) Because the prohibition is nahy li dhatihi
B) Because the prohibition is nahy li ghayrihi
C) Because the hadith commands raj'ah
D) Because it is not actually prohibited

Key Takeaway
A prohibition that is extrinsic to the act (nahy li ghayrihi) does not nullify the act's validity; consequently, a divorce during menstruation is effective and the husband is obligated to take his wife back.

Raj'ah After a Menstrual Divorce: Mustahabb or Wajib?
Intra-Hanafi debate on the ruling of raj'ah after a menstrual divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the debate among Hanafi scholars regarding the ruling of raj'ah after a menstrual divorce and identify the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.

Core Idea
Raj'ah after a menstrual divorce is wajib, not just mustahabb, to remove the sin and its effect.

This lesson delves into an internal Hanafi debate: after a sinful divorce during menstruation, is it merely recommended to take one's wife back, or is it obligatory? The passage presents both views, and the author of al-Hidayah prefers the position of obligation (wajib) based on the plain meaning of the imperative and the principle of removing sin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State that some mashayikh hold raj'ah is mustahabb; the asahh view is that it is wajib.
2
Examine the dalil for istihbab
The hadith's imperative 'flieraji'ha' indicates recommendation, and raj'ah is a right of the husband, so no obligation.
3
Examine the dalil for wujub
A plain imperative indicates obligation; additionally, removing sin is wajib, and the only way to remove the sin of this divorce is to nullify its effect (the 'iddah) through raj'ah.
4
Determine the tarjih
The text states 'the correct view is wajib' (al-asahh annahu wajib). This is the mufta bihi.

و اذا طلق الرجل امرأته فى حالة الحيض وقع الطلاق لان النهى عنه لمعنى فى غيره وهو ما ذكرنا فلا ينعدم مشروعيته ويستحب له ان يراجعها لقوله عليه السلام لعمر مرا بنك فليراجعها وقد طلقها في حالة الحيض وهذا يفيد الوقوع والحث على الرجعة ثم الاستحباب قول بعض المشائخ والاصح انه واجب عملا بحقيقة الامر ورفعا للمعصية بالقدر الممكن برفع اثره وهى العدة ودفعا لضرر تطويل العدة
ترجمہ اور جب مرد نے اپنی بیوی کو حالتِ حیض میں طلاق دی تو طلاق واقع ہو گئی۔ کیونکہ نہیں (حالت حیض میں ) طلاق سے معنی لغیرہ کی وجہ سے ہے اور وہ معنی وہ ہیں جو ہم نے ذکر کئے ۔ پس اس کی مشروعیت معدوم نہیں ہوگی۔ اور مرد کیلئے مستحب ہے کہ عورت سے مراجعت کر لے۔ ( حضرت ) عمر سے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ اپنے بیٹے کو حکم دو۔ وہ (اپنی بیوی ) سے مراجعت کر لے۔ حال یہ کہ اس نے اس کو حالت حیض میں طلاق دی ہے۔ اور یہ ( قول نبی ) فائدہ دیتا ہے ( حالتِ حیض میں ) وقوع طلاق کا۔ اور رجعت پر آمادہ کرنے کا پھر استحباب بعض مشائخ کا قول ہے۔ اور اصبح یہ ہے کہ واجب ہے حقیقت امر پر عمل کرتے ہوئے اور بقد را مکان معصیت کے اثر کو اٹھاتے ہوئے طلاق کے اثر کو اٹھا کر اور وہ عدت ہے اور تطویل عدت کے ضرر کو دفع کرنے کیلئے۔
تشریح مسئلہ اگر کسی مرد نے حالت حیض میں اپنی منکوحہ کو طلاق دے دی تو طلاق واقع ہوگئی اور بالا جماع طلاق دینے والا گنہگار ہوگا ۔ وقوع طلاق کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حالت حیض میں طلاق سے نہبی معنی لغیرہ کی وجہ سے اور وہ معنی لغیر و تطویل عدت ہے۔ یعنی حالت حیض میں طلاق دینے کی صورت میں عورت کی عدت طویل ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ جس حیض میں طلاق دی گئی وہ عدت میں شمار نہیں ہو گا۔ اور اسی طرح اس کے بعد والا ہر شمار نہیں ہو گا۔ حاصل یہ کہ حالت حیض میں طلاق سے نہی، نہی لغیرہ ہے نہ کہ نہی لذاتہ اور نہی لغیرہ سے مشروع لذاتہ باقی رہتا ہے۔ اس وجہ سے ہم نے کہا کہ حالت حیض میں طلاق کی نفس مشروعیت معدوم نہیں ہوئی۔ صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ اس مرد کیلئے اپنی اس بیوی سے مراجعت کرنا مستحب ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب عبد اللہ ابن عمر نے حالت حیض میں طلاق دے دی تو حضرت عمر نے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے اس کے بارے میں دریافت فرمایا تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا کہ اپنے بیٹے عبداللہ کو کم کرو کہ وہ اس سے رجعت کرے۔ اس حدیث سے دو باتیں مستفاد ہوئیں ۔ ایک تو یہ کہ حالت حیض میں طلاق دینے سے طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ اگر حالت حیض میں طالق واقع نہ ہوتی تو ابن عمر گور جعت کا حکم دینے کے کیا معنی ہیں ۔ دوسری بات یہ کہ اس حدیث میں مراجعت پر آمادہ کیا گیا ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ رجعت کے استحباب کے قائل بعض مشائخ ہیں اور صحیح قول یہ ہے کہ رجعت واجب ہے۔ دلیل استحباب یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں فلیر اجحها صیغہ امر ہے۔ اور امر کا ادنیٰ مرتبہ استباب ہے۔ اور یہاں استحباب پر قرینہ بھی موجود ہے۔ قرینہ یہ ہے کہ رجعت خالص شوہر کا حق ہے اور انسان پر اپنے حق میں کوئی وجوب نہیں ہوتا۔ وجوب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مطلق امر وجوب کیلئے ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا حدیث میں بھی صیغہ امر وجوب کیلئے ہوگا۔ پس وجوب مراد لینے کی صورت میں حقیقت امر پر عمل ہو گیا اور جعت اسلئے بھی واجب ہے کہ حالت حیض میں طلاق دینا معصیت ہے۔ اور معصیت کا اٹھانا واجب ہے۔ تفصیل یہ ہے کہ حالت حیض میں طلاق واقع کرنا : معصیت ہے۔ پس مناسب تو یہ تھا کہ نفس طلاق اور مین طلاق کو اٹھا لیا جاتا۔ لیکن چونکہ نفس طلاں کو اٹھا ناممکن نہیں اس لئے ہم کہتے ہیں کہ کم از کم اسکے اثر ہی کو اٹھا لیا جائے ۔ اور طلاق کا اثر عدت ہے پس حاصل یہ کہ رجعت کر کے عدت کو مرتفع کر دیا جائے تا کہ بقدر امکان معصیت کا رفع ہو سکے۔ اور رجعت اسلئے بھی واجب ہے کہ رجعت کی وجہ سے عورت سے تطویل عدت کا نسر ختم ہو جاتا ہے۔
And when a man divorces his wife during menstruation, the divorce occurs because the prohibition is for a reason extrinsic to it (ma'na fi ghayrihi), which we have mentioned, so its legitimacy is not nullified. And it is recommended for him to take her back (yuraji'uha) due to his saying (peace be upon him) to 'Umar: 'Command your son to take her back' while he had divorced her during menstruation. This indicates occurrence (wuqu') and encouragement of reconciliation (raj'ah). Then recommendation (istihbab) is the saying of some mashayikh, and the correct view is that it is obligatory (wajib) in accordance with the reality of the matter, and to remove sin to the extent possible by removing its effect, which is the 'iddah, and to ward off the harm of prolonging the 'iddah. Translation: And when a man divorces his wife during menstruation, the divorce occurs... (Urdu translation follows). Explanation of the issue: If a man divorces his wife during menstruation, the divorce occurs and the divorcer is sinful by consensus. ...
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning divorce during menstruation. It establishes that such a divorce is effective (waqi') despite being prohibited. The reason is that the prohibition is due to an extrinsic factor (ma'na fi ghayrihi) — namely, prolonging the 'iddah — not because the act itself is inherently evil. Therefore the legitimacy (mashru'iyyah) of the divorce remains. The husband is then encouraged to take his wife back (raj'ah). The text presents a debate among Hanafi scholars: Some mashayikh hold that raj'ah is only recommended (mustahabb), while the correct view (asahh) is that it is obligatory (wajib). The evidence for istihbab is that the command in the hadith (فلي راجعها) is in the imperative form, which at minimum indicates recommendation, and there is a qarinah (contextual factor) that raj'ah is the husband's right, and no one is obliged to exercise his own right. The argument for wujub is that a plain imperative indicates obligation, and moreover, giving divorce during hayd is a sin; removing sin is obligatory, and since the divorce itself cannot be undone, its effect (the 'iddah) must be removed through raj'ah. The passage also cites the famous incident of 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar, which proves both the occurrence of divorce and the command for raj'ah.

Key Terms
نہی لغیرہ (nahy li ghayrihi): A prohibition due to an extrinsic factor, not because the act is inherently evil. The act's legitimacy remains.
رجعت (raj'ah): The husband taking back his wife during the 'iddah period after a revocable divorce.
معصیت (ma'siyah): Sin. The act of divorcing during menstruation is sinful but the divorce itself is valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Hidayah, what is the ruling on raj'ah after a divorce given during menstruation?
A) Mustahabb
B) Wajib
C) Haram
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that raj'ah after a menstrual divorce is obligatory (wajib) to remove the sin and its effect on the 'iddah.
